
============== high level task decomposition ================
[{'objective': 'Calculate the volume of tetrahedron ABCD using the given edge lengths.'}, {'objective': 'Compute the total surface area of tetrahedron ABCD by finding the area of each triangular face.'}, {'objective': 'Use the formula for the inradius of a tetrahedron (inradius = 3 * volume / surface area) to find the equal distance from point I to each face.'}, {'objective': 'Simplify the inradius expression into the form (m√n)/p and find the sum m + n + p.'}]
============== task analysis ================
1. Extract and Summarize Given Information:
- The problem involves a tetrahedron named ABCD.
- Edge lengths are given with specific equalities:
  * AB = CD = √41
  * AC = BD = √80
  * BC = AD = √89
- There exists a point I inside the tetrahedron such that the perpendicular distances from I to each of the four faces are equal.
- The common distance from I to each face can be expressed in the form (m√n)/p, where m, n, p are positive integers, m and p are coprime, and n is square-free.

2. Analyze Relationships Between Components:
- The tetrahedron has pairs of edges equal in length, suggesting some symmetry or special geometric property.
- The equalities AB=CD, AC=BD, and BC=AD imply a pairing of opposite edges with equal lengths.
- The point I is equidistant from all faces, indicating that I is the incenter of the tetrahedron (the center of the inscribed sphere).
- The equal distance to faces corresponds to the inradius of the tetrahedron.
- The problem’s structure relies on the interplay between edge lengths and the incenter’s position.
- The constraints on m, n, p indicate the final answer should be simplified to lowest terms with a square-free radical.

3. Identify the Field of Study:
- The problem lies primarily in solid geometry (3D Euclidean geometry).
- It involves concepts of tetrahedra, distances from points to planes, and properties of incenters and inscribed spheres.
- Algebraic manipulation and possibly vector geometry or coordinate geometry may be involved.
- Such problems are common in mathematical competitions and advanced geometry studies.

4. Highlight Aspects Needing Clarification:
- The problem does not specify the coordinates or angles of the tetrahedron, only edge lengths and equalities.
- It assumes the tetrahedron is well-defined and non-degenerate with the given edge lengths.
- The existence of point I inside the tetrahedron with equal distances to faces is stated, but the uniqueness or method to find it is not detailed.
- Potential challenges include verifying the tetrahedron’s existence with given edge lengths and computing the inradius without explicit coordinates.
- The problem requires careful handling of radicals and simplification to meet the form constraints.

async def forward(self, taskInfo):
    from collections import Counter
    print("Task Requirement: ", taskInfo)
    sub_tasks = []
    agents = []
    logs = []

    cot_instruction_1 = "Sub-task 1: Identify and list all given edge lengths and their equalities, and interpret the geometric implications of these equalities on the tetrahedron's structure without attempting calculations." 
    cot_agent_1 = LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Chain-of-Thought Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)
    subtask_desc1 = {
        "subtask_id": "subtask_1",
        "instruction": cot_instruction_1,
        "context": ["user query"],
        "agent_collaboration": "CoT"
    }
    thinking1, answer1 = await cot_agent_1([taskInfo], cot_instruction_1, is_sub_task=True)
    agents.append(f"CoT agent {cot_agent_1.id}, analyzing given edge lengths, thinking: {thinking1.content}; answer: {answer1.content}")
    sub_tasks.append(f"Sub-task 1 output: thinking - {thinking1.content}; answer - {answer1.content}")
    subtask_desc1['response'] = {"thinking": thinking1, "answer": answer1}
    logs.append(subtask_desc1)
    print("Step 1: ", sub_tasks[-1])

    cot_sc_instruction_2 = "Sub-task 2: Determine the pairs of opposite edges and verify the symmetry conditions implied by the equalities AB=CD, AC=BD, and BC=AD, establishing the tetrahedron's special properties." 
    N_sc = self.max_sc

    possible_answers_2 = []
    possible_thinkings_2 = []
    subtask_desc2 = {
        "subtask_id": "subtask_2",
        "instruction": cot_sc_instruction_2,
        "context": ["user query", thinking1.content],
        "agent_collaboration": "SC_CoT"
    }

        thinking2, answer2 = await cot_agents_2[i]([taskInfo, thinking1], cot_sc_instruction_2, is_sub_task=True)
        agents.append(f"CoT-SC agent {cot_agents_2[i].id}, verifying symmetry conditions, thinking: {thinking2.content}; answer: {answer2.content}")
        possible_answers_2.append(answer2)
        possible_thinkings_2.append(thinking2)

To express the volume in terms of the given edge lengths and symmetry, a natural approach is to use the Cayley-Menger determinant formula for the volume of a tetrahedron given its six edge lengths. The Cayley-Menger determinant V is given by:\n\nV^2 = (1/288) * det(M),\n\nwhere M is the 5x5 matrix:\n\nM =\n| 0    1       1       1       1     |\n| 1    0     AB^2    AC^2    AD^2   |\n| 1  AB^2     0     BC^2    BD^2   |\n| 1  AC^2   BC^2      0     CD^2   |\n| 1  AD^2   BD^2    CD^2      0    |\n\nUsing the given edge lengths:\nAB^2 = 41, AC^2 = 80, AD^2 = 89,\nBC^2 = 89, BD^2 = 80, CD^2 = 41.\n\nSubstituting these into M, the determinant can be computed to find V^2, and thus V = sqrt(V^2).\n\nThis formula fully expresses the volume in terms of the given edge lengths and respects the symmetry conditions.     print("Task Requirement: ", taskInfo)
    sub_tasks = []
    agents = []
    logs = []

    # Stage 1: Analyze given edge lengths and geometric implications (SC_CoT)

        "Sub-task 1: Identify and list all given edge lengths and their equalities explicitly. "

    )
    cot_agents_1 = [LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Chain-of-Thought Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0) for _ in range(self.max_sc)]
    possible_answers_1 = []
    possible_thinkings_1 = []
    subtask_desc_1 = {
        "subtask_id": "subtask_1",
        "instruction": cot_sc_instruction_1,
        "context": ["user query"],
        "agent_collaboration": "SC_CoT"
    }
    for i in range(self.max_sc):
        thinking1, answer1 = await cot_agents_1[i]([taskInfo], cot_sc_instruction_1, is_sub_task=True)
        agents.append(f"CoT-SC agent {cot_agents_1[i].id}, analyzing given edges and symmetry, thinking: {thinking1.content}; answer: {answer1.content}")
        possible_answers_1.append(answer1)
        possible_thinkings_1.append(thinking1)
    final_decision_agent_1 = LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Final Decision Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)
    thinking1, answer1 = await final_decision_agent_1([taskInfo] + possible_thinkings_1, "Sub-task 1: Synthesize and choose the most consistent answer for given edges and symmetry.", is_sub_task=True)
